  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_135b246d-a10d-4151-9845-a075c06dd59c'

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer17018051865631219102">Reşat Nuri Güntekin'in 1922 yılında ilk kez Vakit gazetesinde tefrika edilen en tanınmış eseridir. Fransız Lisesi mezunu gencecik, delişmen bir kız olan Feride'nin serüveni yaşadığı derin bir hayal kırıklığı sonrasında nişanlısını, ailesini İstanbul'da bırakarak Anadolu'nun küçük bir köyüne öğretmen olmasıyla başlar. Daha sonra bu köyü diğer kasabalar, şehirler izler. Önce</span>
  <span id="freeText17018051865631219102" style="display:none">Reşat Nuri Güntekin'in 1922 yılında ilk kez Vakit gazetesinde tefrika edilen en tanınmış eseridir. Fransız Lisesi mezunu gencecik, delişmen bir kız olan Feride'nin serüveni yaşadığı derin bir hayal kırıklığı sonrasında nişanlısını, ailesini İstanbul'da bırakarak Anadolu'nun küçük bir köyüne öğretmen olmasıyla başlar. Daha sonra bu köyü diğer kasabalar, şehirler izler. Önceleri her gittiği yerde Kurtuluş Savaşı'nın etkileri görülür, güç koşulların, sefaletin izlerine rastlanır. Sonraları farklı kültürden gelen genç, yalnız ve bağımsız bir kızın toplumsal yaşamdaki zorlukları, çatışan değer yargıları, karşısına dikilen çıkar ilişkileri, Feride'nin iç dünyasındaki fırtınalar ve derin yalnızlıkla iç içe geçerek okurun karşısına çıkar. Çalıkuşu, gerçekçi yönelimin ilk dönemlerinden olan bir başyapıttır.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17018051865631219102" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>

  <span id="freeText5682782085103147027" style="display:none">I've read this book more than three times. I don't own it but my aunt has it on her bookshelf. <br /> It is a wonderful story about a girl growing up and experiencing love, broken heart and even naiveness.<br />Calikusu, thus called after a bird for her endless energy and beauty, is an orphan. She lives with her aunts and uncles and is finally engaged to his cousin. She loves him in her pure-hearted way but the age gap leaves her at school while he is away for work in a foreign country.<br />Little before the wedding a woman comes and tells he cheated on her and asks in the name of her friend for Calikusu to set him free. That she does and leaves the house and her family, leaving only a note behind.<br /> Years pass, we can follow her growing up, experiencing difficulties and a loss of a child - though single, she adopted a neglected girl. She then meets a kind older doctor whom she marries. After the death of her husband, Calikusu finally returns to her family. They have missed her, looked for her, blamed her former bethored. But now Calikusu is back, though sadder, more weary. But the kind doctor has made a gift before his death - he reveals Calikusus secrets to her family and thus they trap her- this time in a loving marriage. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8377181001055799264">My first approach to turkish literature, and I loved it.<br/><br/>This novel is a masterpiece, very rich .<br/>The characters’ development and the plot progress is outstanding.<br/>It is filled with raw emotions.<br/>The main character is very unique, I love her so much.<br/><br/>I usually rate my books on the amount of tears I shed on,,<br/>And I wept a lot on this one.<br/><br/>I highly recommend it.<br/><br/></span>

<div id="review_2247610015" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2247610015" />
    <a title="Roman Kurys" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48577145-roman-kurys"><img alt="Roman Kurys" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591566555p2/48577145.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2247610015?book_show_action=true">Jul 29, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Roman Kurys" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Roman Kurys" href="/user/show/48577145-roman-kurys">Roman Kurys</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2247610015" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer396043864833176089">I was torn with the rating for “Calicusu”. It was really a good book at heart. It is filled with emotional distress of a privileged girl who is thrown into the real world, to grow up and get a taste of reality on her own.<br/>There is a lot of good scenes here, lots of good parts that did stir up emotion in my black heart, but there was just way too much fluff and unnecessary (to me) details which did nothing else but bore me. <br/><br/>Characters: 2<br/>This could just be me, but I simply could not find myself car</span>
  <span id="freeText396043864833176089" style="display:none">I was torn with the rating for “Calicusu”. It was really a good book at heart. It is filled with emotional distress of a privileged girl who is thrown into the real world, to grow up and get a taste of reality on her own.<br />There is a lot of good scenes here, lots of good parts that did stir up emotion in my black heart, but there was just way too much fluff and unnecessary (to me) details which did nothing else but bore me. <br /><br />Characters: 2<br />This could just be me, but I simply could not find myself caring enough about any of the characters here. Looking back at it, I can actually say that there really is just one character: Calicusu. The rest wears kind of like a supporting cast of ever changing people coming and going to cause her grief or some happiness. Or sometimes do nothing at all to the story, just serve as a filler for Feride’s journal entry. <br />It gives a glimpse into her psyche, sure does! However I have to care about Feride, to care about glimpses into her psyche, and with exception of a few moments, I did not. <br />Call me heartless. Fine. I deserved it. <br /><br />Plot: 2<br />Plot..was... There was no plot. There was random roaming for no reason at all. She could have prevented it all, the entire book, by just staying. She actually appears like a spoiled rich girl, who grew up in privilege and is forcing herself to live out some years in misery due to no one else but herself and her silly, illogical whimsies. <br />I cannot understand Feride. She does not appear as a strong female character, like I think she is supposed to. She appears to be a completely emotional, illogical, spoiled brat who did not get her way and is now throwing a tantrum. <br /><br />Setting: 3<br />There really was not a whole lot of setting here either. Feride bounced around Turkish small and big cities but the setting played a very small effect to the entire story. Most of the places she was living in, we don’t even know the full names of. That doesn’t help the immersion. <br />What I did like, however, was to see how different Turkish culture was (or still is) from what I am used to. A glimpse into the psyche of Turkish citizens back in early 1900’s was great. That’s the only reason why Setting is a 3 stars. <br /><br />Overall, I would say, if you enjoy novellas, melodramas or in general lots of pages about nothing, this is the book for you. <br />I did not see how or why this became a classic of Turkish literature and if I can avoid reading more books by this author, I will. <br /><br />My personal suggestion is: steer clear of this one, it’s not worth the time. <br /><br /><br />Roman “Ragnar”</span>
  <a data-text-id="396043864833176089" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7346834963215967876">Never thought I would enjoy a romantic story, a novel about love. But oh my stars, did I love this book. This novel made me cry, smile and experience all the feelings you're supposed to feel reading such a book.<br/>The main heroine was really, really nice and I liked her a lot. She felt real (except for her beauty, maybe) and alive. She had her flaws, but she was good and kind, such a lovable character.<br/>Doctor, oh doctor!   <span id="freeText7346834963215967876" style="display:none">Never thought I would enjoy a romantic story, a novel about love. But oh my stars, did I love this book. This novel made me cry, smile and experience all the feelings you're supposed to feel reading such a book.<br />The main heroine was really, really nice and I liked her a lot. She felt real (except for her beauty, maybe) and alive. She had her flaws, but she was good and kind, such a lovable character.<br />Doctor, oh doctor! Even though we got to see him pretty much only in last two parts of the book (which were kinda small), I loved him a lot. He was a friend and a father to our Feride. He was one of the best characters in all creation. I adored him.<br />I can't say I liked Kamran a lot. He was okay, I guess, but I never really rooted for him or understood him. I pretty much felt the same way about him as doctor did. But, he was her choice, so we can't do anything about it. He was, after all, madly in love with her, that's probably why I accepted him.<br />Overall the book is soo good and I don't regret reading it one bit. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10460351737570416259">Heartbreaking. Emotional. I cried when I was reading parts of the book, I felt everything Feride felt. And I couldn't let go. I wish it was not over. Such a heartbreaking story, beautifully written.<br/><br/>The book also provides an insight of Turkish society in Anatolia in the early 20th century.   <span id="freeText10460351737570416259" style="display:none">Heartbreaking. Emotional. I cried when I was reading parts of the book, I felt everything Feride felt. And I couldn't let go. I wish it was not over. Such a heartbreaking story, beautifully written.<br /><br />The book also provides an insight of Turkish society in Anatolia in the early 20th century. The way women were treated, no equality, no independence. I was amazed how people's attitude towards somebody, their gossiping and beliefs can ruin somebody's life. It also provided an interesting point of the covers women sometimes wear on their faces. It doesn't have to be of religious reasons, but to hide from the inappropriate looks of other people. Feride, the main character, is cursed with beauty that gets her into trouble through the whole story.<br /><br />I highly recommend this book to anybody who likes emotional stories!</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1059955606" />
    <a title="Alexandra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5862149-alexandra"><img alt="Alexandra" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1312574609p2/5862149.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1059955606?book_show_action=true">Sep 20, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alexandra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alexandra" href="/user/show/5862149-alexandra">Alexandra</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1059955606" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1468258905877181459">This was my first ever piece of Turkish literature and by far one of the greatest literary surprises! I wasn't expecting to devour every page and literally hold my breath to the very end. I'm not even sure what was more impressive: the delightful writing flow, the witty dialogues, the superb insight of the falling Ottoman culture or the most delicate and highly accurate portrayal of feminine psychology. It was unbelievably enjoyable and left me somehow yearning for more. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2568270961" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2568270961?book_show_action=true">Jan 13, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robyn Brailey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robyn Brailey" href="/user/show/41874175-robyn-brailey">Robyn Brailey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/41952880-aliku-u-the-wren">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41874175-robyn-brailey?shelf=favourite-ever-books">favourite-ever-books</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2568270961" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1005189518607911660">I came across a new phenomenon whilst reading this book. Typically when I find a book I love, and let it be clear that I love this book, I become hooked and I cannot put it down until it is complete. With Çalikusu, there were times where I had to force myself to stop, because i wanted to savour the story. I didn't want it to end.<br/><br/>The writing is beautiful and it is impossible not to adore the character of Feridé, who is just so believable to me even despite the different era in which she is writte</span>
  <span id="freeText1005189518607911660" style="display:none">I came across a new phenomenon whilst reading this book. Typically when I find a book I love, and let it be clear that I love this book, I become hooked and I cannot put it down until it is complete. With Çalikusu, there were times where I had to force myself to stop, because i wanted to savour the story. I didn't want it to end.<br /><br />The writing is beautiful and it is impossible not to adore the character of Feridé, who is just so believable to me even despite the different era in which she is written. I'm sure she will forever remain as one of my all time most loved characters.<br /><br />Exactly like the editor of this version, I first came across Çalikusu on Netflix (where it is named Lovebird). I loved the characters almost instantly (I was so pleased when later reading the book to realise Feridé was played to perfection). Whilst watching, I did some research, learning the show was based on a popular book. I knew, that as soon as I finished the show, I would want to read it. Unfortunately the show was cancelled before the story was completed, making me even more desperate to read the book to know Feridé and Kâmran's ending. As soon as I finished the show, I looked for a way to buy the book, but I could not find a copy of the original translation. Luckily I decided to search again a few months later, discovering this new translation had just been published. I am so grateful! It does not disappoint.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1005189518607911660" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2720067078188863593">I read this book (well, a translated edition) when I was in school, which was a looong time ago :)))<br/>I remember going to a book store one day on my way from school... I was looking through stacks of different books, randomly picking whatever had looked interesting.   <span id="freeText2720067078188863593" style="display:none">I read this book (well, a translated edition) when I was in school, which was a looong time ago :)))<br />I remember going to a book store one day on my way from school... I was looking through stacks of different books, randomly picking whatever had looked interesting. I saw this blue cover with a drawing of a pretty yet funny looking girl, and a lovebirds... for some reason something enigmatic was in that simple drawing... I opened the first page... and I never put the book down for the next two days... I laughed, I cried, I couldn't leave the book down, because I absolutely HAD to know what had happened next...<br />It is a fairy tale really, but a nice one.<br />Very beautifully, very romantically narrated. Guntekin created a wonderful, magic-like vision of Turkey and love.<br />Yet there's a lot to learn from the story of young Feride, it's not just an airy love story. Women's rights, customs, independence, forgiveness... <br />It became one of those books that I would pick up off the shelf many, many times and re-read again, again and again...<br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_1825606030" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1825606030" />
    <a title="Anissa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7530978-anissa"><img alt="Anissa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1498839717p2/7530978.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1825606030?book_show_action=true">Nov 29, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anissa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anissa" href="/user/show/7530978-anissa">Anissa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7530978-anissa?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7530978-anissa?shelf=too-many-feels">too-many-feels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7530978-anissa?shelf=tv-film-related">tv-film-related</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7530978-anissa?shelf=1920s">1920s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7530978-anissa?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1825606030" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3557977699813317284">A friend of mine recommended the 2013 TV series based on this book (which ended up getting cancelled) awhile back. It was tough to find an English edition of the book or the show with subtitles (it's on Netflix now though!), but I was able to find a copy at my uni library! I so wish I was able to read it in the original Turkish (some things are lost in translation - especially when it comes to such a beautiful language), because it's a really lovely story.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2566888034" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2566888034" />
    <a title="Anna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32926679-anna"><img alt="Anna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1534455052p2/32926679.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2566888034?book_show_action=true">Oct 19, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anna" href="/user/show/32926679-anna">Anna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 5170167563" href="/book/show/18003978--">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32926679-anna?shelf=2010-and-earlier">2010-and-earlier</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32926679-anna?shelf=all-kinds-of-love">all-kinds-of-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32926679-anna?shelf=authors-from-around-the-world">authors-from-around-the-world</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32926679-anna?shelf=female-protagonist">female-protagonist</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32926679-anna?shelf=read-in-russian">read-in-russian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32926679-anna?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32926679-anna?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32926679-anna?shelf=male-author">male-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32926679-anna?shelf=coming-of-age">coming-of-age</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32926679-anna?shelf=turkish">turkish</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2566888034" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17955874996774916685">This book is an absolute masterpiece and it's really a pity that it doesn't seem to be in print in English. It is both a love story and a bildungsroman and an exploration of vast change happening in a country. I was so impressed by this novel that I wrote a poem about it (not going to share but it just goes to explaining how much it meant to me). Highly recommended!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Irena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Irena" href="/user/show/2250136-irena">Irena</a>

        rated it

<span id="freeTextContainer3423251362686303542">I read the Russian translation of this book when I was a pre-teen at least 20 times.           </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('zO7VIFMv0FMsG4t45Lwd+nny0SCSjDeK/6yljfTcZX26Mxq/lFBX12apbeBnlb/Fybhh+fyADTCpH5Uh1F3XZw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('n0oNRjjiLcUZ85SAiE/9WsKjFR3MVTXSTODXBule0D3pl8LZ/52qQVNBchgLZl9lcumlxKJZD2gaU+eqyd9iJw==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

Hayatında asıl aradığı şeyin Muazzez olmadığını biliyordu, fakat Muazzez olmadan bunu aramaya muktedir olamayacağını sanıyordu.&quot;\n\nKuyucaklı Yusuf, Türk edebiyatının belki de en romantik kahramanıdır. Hayatın ve insanların zalimliği karşısındaki naif duruşu ile bir yandan trajik bir sona ilerlerken, bir yandan da yaşadığı lirik aşk hikayesinin kahramanı olarak edebiyat tarihinde yerini almıştır.\n\nSabahattin Ali büyük romanı Kuyucaklı Yusuf\'ta lirik ve romantik bir kahramanın yanı sıra, zalim ve ağulu bir taşra portresini bütün aktörleriyle gözümüzde canlandırır.<\/span>\n  <a       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/3044063.Re_at_Nuri_G_ntekin">About Reşat Nuri Güntekin</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/3044063.Re_at_Nuri_G_ntekin"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1527947500p3/3044063.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/3044063.Re_at_Nuri_G_ntekin">Reşat Nuri Güntekin
</a></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer14917134662350687545">Reşat Nuri Güntekin (Istanbul, 25 November 1889 - London, 13 December 1956) was a Turkish novelist, storywriter and playwright. His novel, Çalıkuşu ("The Wren", 1922) is about the destiny of a young Turkish female teacher in Anatolia; the movie was filmed on this book in 1966, and remade as TV series in 1986. His narrative has a detailed and precise style, with a realistic tone. His other signific</span>
  <span id="freeText14917134662350687545" style="display:none">Reşat Nuri Güntekin (Istanbul, 25 November 1889 - London, 13 December 1956) was a Turkish novelist, storywriter and playwright. His novel, Çalıkuşu ("The Wren", 1922) is about the destiny of a young Turkish female teacher in Anatolia; the movie was filmed on this book in 1966, and remade as TV series in 1986. His narrative has a detailed and precise style, with a realistic tone. His other significant novels include Yeşil Gece ("Green Night") and Yaprak Dökümü ("The Fall Of Leaves")<br /><br />Biography<br /><br />His father was a major in the army. Reşat Nuri attended primary school in Çanakkale, the Çanakkale Secondary School and the İzmir School of Freres. He graduated from Istanbul University, Faculty of Literature in 1912. He worked as a teacher and administrator at high schools in Bursa and Istanbul, then as an inspector at the Ministry of National Education (1931). He served as the deputy of Çanakkale between 1933 and 1943 in the Turkish Parliament, the chief inspector at the Ministry of National Education (1947), and a cultural attaché to Paris (1950), when he was also the Turkish representative to UNESCO.<br /><br />After his retirement, he served at the literary board of the Istanbul Municipal Theatres. He died in London, where he had gone to be treated for his lung cancer. He is buried at the Karacaahmet Cemetery in İstanbul.</span>
